id=\"artAbst\" class=\"collapse-blocked\">Abstract</h2>\n        <!-- Start article video abstract -->\n\t<!-- End article video abstract -->\n\t<div class=\"article-text wd-jnl-art-abstract cf\" itemprop=\"description\">\n                      <P>We identify a strong lensing galaxy in the cluster IRC 0218 (also known as XMM-LSS J02182\u201305102) that is spectroscopically confirmed to be at <I>z</I> = 1.62, making it the highest-redshift strong lens galaxy known. The lens is one of the two brightest cluster galaxies and lenses a background source galaxy into an arc and a counterimage. With <I>Hubble Space Telescope</I> (<I>HST</I>) grism and Keck/LRIS spectroscopy, we measure the source redshift to be <I>z</I>             <SUB>S</SUB> = 2.26. Using <I>HST</I> imaging in ACS/F475W, ACS/F814W, WFC3/F125W, and WFC3/F160W, we model the lens mass distribution with an elliptical power-law profile and account for the effects of the cluster halo and nearby galaxies. The Einstein radius is <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"$\\theta _{\\rm E}=0.38^{+0.02}_{-0.01}$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/apjl497422ieqn1.gif\"></IMG> arcsec (<IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"$3.2_{-0.1}^{+0.2}$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/apjl497422ieqn2.gif\"></IMG> kpc) and the total enclosed mass is <I>M</I>             <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"$_{\\rm tot} ({&lt;} \\theta _{\\rm E})=1.8^{+0.2}_{-0.1}\\times 10^{11} \\,M_{\\odot }$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/apjl497422ieqn3.gif\"></IMG>. We estimate that the cluster environment contributes ~10% of this total mass. Assuming a Chabrier initial mass function (IMF), the dark matter fraction within \u03b8<SUB>E</SUB> is <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"$f_{\\rm DM}^{{\\rm Chab}} = 0.3_{-0.3}^{+0.1}$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/apjl497422ieqn4.gif\"></IMG>, while a Salpeter IMF is marginally inconsistent with the enclosed mass (<IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"$f_{\\rm DM}^{{\\rm Salp}} = -0.3_{-0.5}^{+0.2}$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/apjl497422ieqn5.gif\"></IMG>). The total magnification of the source is <IMG ALIGN=\"MIDDLE\" alt=\"$\\mu _{\\rm tot}=2.1_{-0.3}^{+0.4}$\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/apjl497422ieqn6.gif\"></IMG>. The source has at least one bright compact region offset from the source center. Emission from Ly\u03b1 and [O <span class=\"small-caps\">III</span>] are likely to probe different regions in the source.</P>       </div>\n    <!-- End abstract -->\n<!-- Start Export citation and abstract tools -->\n\t<p>\n\t\t<small>Export citation and abstract</small>\n\t\t<span class=\"btn-multi-block\">\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=2041-8205/789/2/L31&doi=10.1088/2041-8205/789/2/L31&exportFormat=iopexport_bib&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-bib\" title=\"Export BibTex\">BibTeX</a>\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=2041-8205/789/2/L31&doi=10.1088/2041-8205/789/2/L31&exportFormat=iopexport_ris&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-ris\" title=\"Export RIS\">RIS</a>\n\t\t</span>\n\t</p>\n<!-- End Export citation and abstract tools -->\n<!-- Start AAS Related Links -->\n<div class=\"reveal-container reveal-closed reveal-plus-icon bdt-1 mt-2 mb-2 wd-jnl-art-article-aas-related-links\">\n  <div class=\"replica-h3 mt-0\">\n    <a href=\"#\" class=\"reveal-trigger\" data-reveal-label-alt=\"Hide related links\">Related links</a>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"reveal-content\">\n    <div class=\"article-meta\"> \n      <ul>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2014ApJ...789L..31W\" target=\"_blank\">NASA ADS Record <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://nedwww.ipac.caltech.edu/cgi-bin/nph-objsearch?refcode=2014ApJ...789L..31W&search_type=Search \" target=\"_blank\">NED Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://simbad.u-strasbg.fr/simbad/sim-ref?querymethod=bib&simbo=on&bibcode=2014ApJ...789L..31W\" target=\"_blank\">Simbad Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"/journal/2041-8205/page/About%20Related%20Links\" target=\"_blank\">About Related Links</a></li>\n      \t</ul>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<!-- Start info bottom -->\n    <!-- End info bottom -->\n<!-- Start article full text -->\n\t<div xmlns:book=\"http://api.iop.org/Book/1.0/\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-full-text article-text\">\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjl497422s1\" name=\"apjl497422s1\">1.\u00a0INTRODUCTION</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Gravitational lensing is a powerful tool for studying the mass structure of galaxies. Lensing studies of early-type galaxies (ETGs) at <em>z</em> &lt; 1 have produced interesting results on their properties. Their total mass density profile slope \u03b3' (where <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn7.gif\" alt=\"$\\rho (r)\\propto r^{-\\gamma ^{\\prime }}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\rho (r)\\propto r^{-\\gamma ^{\\prime }}</script></span></span>) depends solely on the surface stellar mass density at fixed redshift, whereas \u03b3' of individual galaxies does not evolve significantly (Koopmans et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r13\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r13\">2006</a>; Barnab\u00e8 et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r2\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r2\">2013</a>; Sonnenfeld et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r29\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r29\">2013</a>). ETGs also favor a heavier stellar initial mass function (IMF; Auger et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r1\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r1\">2010</a>; Sonnenfeld et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r28\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r28\">2012</a>). Nonetheless, the evolution of the mass distribution of ETGs at <em>z</em> &gt; 1 is not well constrained. Identifying strong lensing galaxies at <em>z</em> &gt; 1 provides leverage on how ETGs assemble and tests the current cosmological paradigm.</p><p>However, strong lensing galaxies are increasingly rare at higher redshifts due to the evolving galaxy mass function, decreasing background volume, and decreasing lensing efficiency. Distant lenses also require high-resolution imaging to separate the source and lensing galaxy, and near-infrared spectroscopy to confirm their redshifts. van der Wel et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r37\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r37\">2013</a>) reported the most distant strong lensing galaxy known thus far at <em>z</em><sub>L</sub> = 1.53 and estimated one <em>z</em><sub>L</sub> &gt; 1 system per ~200\u2009arcmin<sup>2</sup>.</p><p>Here, we report the discovery of a strong lensing galaxy embedded in a cluster at <em>z</em> = 1.62 (Papovich et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r23\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r23\">2010</a>; Tanaka et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r33\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r33\">2010</a>), making it the highest-redshift strong lens galaxy known (in contrast with the highest-redshift strong lens cluster at <em>z</em> = 1.75; Gonzalez et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r9\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r9\">2012</a>). The system is unusual because of the high lens redshift, and the lens being the most massive cluster member. The system lies in the Ultra-Deep Survey (UDS) legacy field, which has extensive multi-wavelength observations (Lawrence et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r15\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r15\">2007</a>; Galametz et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r8\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r8\">2013</a>; Skelton et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r27\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r27\">2014</a>). Spectroscopy taken with the <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> (<em>HST</em>) grisms and the Low Resolution Imaging Spectrometer (LRIS; Oke et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r21\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r21\">1995</a>) on Keck confirm the source redshift of <em>z</em><sub>S</sub> = 2.26. We combine the data sets to model the lens, including its environment. We assume \u03a9<sub><em>m</em></sub> = 0.3, \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub> = 0.7, and <em>H</em><sub>0</sub> = 70\u2009km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup>\u2009Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>. All quantities are in <em>h</em><sub>70</sub> units. At <em>z</em> = 1.62, the angular scale is 1'' = 8.47\u2009kpc. We use AB magnitudes.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjl497422s2\" name=\"apjl497422s2\">2.\u00a0OBSERVATIONS</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"apjl497422s2-1\" name=\"apjl497422s2-1\">2.1.\u00a0Keck/LRIS Spectroscopy</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Using the Keck/LRIS, we carried out a spectroscopic survey of the cluster IRC 0218 on 2012 October 19 and 20 (NASA/Keck Program ID 48/2012B). Targets were selected from the Williams et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r38\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r38\">2009</a>) catalog of the UDS taken as part of the UKIRT Infrared Deep Sky Survey (Lawrence et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r15\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r15\">2007</a>). The <em>K</em>-selected catalogs reach 5\u03c3-limiting magnitudes in 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />75 diameter apertures of <em>B</em> &lt; 27.7, <em>R</em> &lt; 27.1, <em>i</em> &lt; 26.8, <em>z</em> &lt; 25.5, <em>J</em> &lt; 23.9, and <em>K</em> &lt; 23.6.</p><p>We use the 600/4000\u2009grism for the blue side and the 600/10000 grating for the red side of LRIS. With 1'' slit widths, the resolutions are 4.0\u2009\u00c5 and 4.7\u2009\u00c5, respectively. Observing conditions were excellent with ~0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />6 median seeing. The total integration time on the lens is 9 hr. We reduce the spectra following Tran et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r34\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r34\">2007</a>), using IRAF<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjl497422fn2\">11</a></sup> routines with custom software provided by D. Kelson (Kelson <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r11\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r11\">2003</a>). The wavelength coverage of the extracted spectra is 3800\u20135800\u2009\u00c5 (blue side) and 7000\u201310000\u2009\u00c5 (red side). A full analysis of this redshift survey will be presented in K.-V. H. Tran et\u00a0al. (in preparation).</p><p>We use XCSAO (Kurtz et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r14\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r14\">1992</a>) with various templates for Lyman-break and Ly\u03b1 emitting galaxies from Shapley et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r26\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r26\">2003</a>) to measure a redshift for the blended spectrum composed of the lens galaxy and the lensed source. The strong emission detected at 3957\u2009\u00c5 (Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl497422f1\">1</a>, top) has the asymmetric profile characteristic of Ly\u03b1 (Shapley et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r26\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r26\">2003</a>) and corresponds to a redshift of <em>z</em><sub>S</sub> = 2.25384 \u00b1 0.00003. The observed Ly\u03b1 equivalent width (EW), derived for a continuum fit between 1180\u20131250\u2009\u00c5 rest frame, is 129.4 \u00b1 4.6\u2009\u00c5.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjl497422f1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjl497422f1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422f1_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 1.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422f1_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 1.</strong>\u00a0Top: total fluxes for the lens system as measured by 3D-HST (object 31684; Skelton et\u00a0al. <a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r27\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r27\">2014</a>) that combines ground-based imaging with <em>HST</em> and <em>Spitzer</em> observations (purple). The best-fit spectral energy distribution from EAZY is included (black). Also shown are the blended Keck/LRIS spectrum (blue) and the <em>HST</em>/WFC3 G102 (green) and G141 (red) grism spectra for the lens. The spectra are arbitrarily normalized for clarity. The grism spectra trace the lens galaxy's Balmer break at <em>z</em><sub>L</sub> = 1.64. The spectra show strong Ly\u03b1 and [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] \u03bb\u03bb4959, 5007 emission from the source at <em>z</em><sub>S</sub> = 2.26. Bottom: filter transmission curves for the <em>HST</em> imaging used in the lens modeling. A bright point source corresponding to emission at <em>z</em><sub>S</sub> = 2.26 is visible in the ACS/F475 (Ly\u03b1) and WFC3/F160 ([O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] \u03bb\u03bb4959, 5007) images.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjl497422f1\" href=\"/2041-8205/789/2/L31/downloadFigure/figure/apjl497422f1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjl497422f1\" href=\"/2041-8205/789/2/L31/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjl497422f1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div><h3 id=\"apjl497422s2-2\" name=\"apjl497422s2-2\">2.2.\u00a0<em>HST</em> Observations</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The UDS cluster falls in a legacy field that has extensive multi-wavelength observations, including deep <em>HST</em> imaging from CANDELS (0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />06 pixel<sup>\u22121</sup>; Grogin et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r10\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r10\">2011</a>; Koekemoer et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r12\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r12\">2011</a>) and G141 spectroscopy from 3D-HST (Brammer et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r3\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r3\">2012</a>). Additional <em>HST</em> imaging and G102 spectroscopy were obtained in GO-12590 (PI: C. Papovich). Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl497422f1\">1</a> shows the total fluxes measured for the more massive of the two brightest cluster galaxies (BCGs) from the 3D-HST catalog of the UDS field (Skelton et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r27\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r27\">2014</a>), which includes <em>Spitzer</em>/IRAC. Hereafter, the BCG refers to this more massive galaxy unless otherwise stated. The BCG shows excess flux at \u03bb &lt; 5000\u2009\u00c5 due to emission from the lensed source. At longer wavelengths, the lens galaxy dominates. Grism spectroscopy confirms the BCG redshift of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn8.gif\" alt=\"$z_{\\rm L}=1.6406^{+0.0018}_{-0.0050}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z_{\\rm L}=1.6406^{+0.0018}_{-0.0050}</script></span></span>. We attribute the redshift difference between the BCG and cluster to peculiar velocities due to the unrelaxed nature of the cluster (e.g., Martel et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r16\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r16\">2014</a>), consistent with the high fraction of star-forming members (Tran et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r35\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r35\">2010</a>). We use <em>z</em> = 1.62 as the lens redshift for cosmological calculations.</p><p>The lens and source are blended in ground-based observations, but <em>HST</em>'s resolution (Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl497422f2\">2</a>) separates the system into the BCG, an arc (object A), and a counterimage (object B). In the grism spectra, the BCG shows strong continuum. Approximately 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5 above the BCG in the G141 spectrum is a compact emission line corresponding to [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] \u03bb\u03bb4959, 5007 at <em>z</em><sub>S</sub> = 2.2623 \u00b1 0.0002 from object A. We also detect [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] \u03bb\u03bb4959, 5007 corresponding to object B once we remove the lens galaxy's light (I. G. Momcheva et\u00a0al. in preparation). The faint object C shows weak [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] \u03bb\u03bb4959, 5007 in the grism spectrum consistent with a redshift of <em>z</em><sub>S</sub> = 2.26.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjl497422f2\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjl497422f2\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422f2_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 2.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 2.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422f2_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 2.</strong>\u00a0Top: negative image of the <em>HST</em> WFC3/G141 grism spectrum for the lensing galaxy (continuum). Approximately ~0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5 above the lens is [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] \u03bb\u03bb4959, 5007 emission from object A at <em>z</em><sub>S</sub> = 2.26. Bottom: false-color image of the UDS cluster core generated with <em>HST</em> imaging (ACS/F475W, ACS/F814W, WFC3/F125W, and WFC3/F160W). North and east are up and left, respectively. Labeled are the BCG lens and the other BCG (Member 2). The inset (3'' <b>&#x00d7;</b> 3'') shows the lens with the arc (A) and counterimage (B) labeled. Another faint galaxy (C) is weakly detected by the grism and consistent with <em>z</em> ~ 2.26. The arrow indicates the dispersion direction of the grism observations (top).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjl497422f2\" href=\"/2041-8205/789/2/L31/downloadFigure/figure/apjl497422f2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjl497422f2\" href=\"/2041-8205/789/2/L31/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjl497422f2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjl497422s3\" name=\"apjl497422s3\">3.\u00a0MODELING THE STRONG LENSING SYSTEM</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Combining our ground-based spectroscopy and <em>HST</em> observations, we confirm that the strong lensing system is composed of the BCG lens and source. We model the system with\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">Glee</span>, a software developed by S. H. Suyu and A. Halkola (Suyu &amp; Halkola <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r30\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r30\">2010</a>; Suyu et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r31\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r31\">2012</a>). Lensing mass distributions are parameterized profiles, and background sources are modeled on a pixel grid (Suyu et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r32\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r32\">2006</a>). The lens galaxy light distributions are modeled as S\u00e9rsic profiles. Unresolved point sources on the pixel grid are modeled as point images on the image plane. Model parameters of the lens and the source are constrained through Markov Chain Monte Carlo (MCMC) sampling.</p><h3 id=\"apjl497422s3-1\" name=\"apjl497422s3-1\">3.1.\u00a0Lens Model</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Taking a 27 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 27 pixel region around the lens, we utilize the deepest <em>HST</em> images spanning the widest wavelength range: ACS/F475W, ACS/F814W, WFC3/F125W, and WFC3/F160W (Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl497422f3\">3</a>, top rows). We model the lens galaxy as an elliptical singular power-law mass distribution with the mass profile slope parameterized as \u0393 = (\u03b3' \u2212 1)/2 (where the three-dimensional mass density is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn9.gif\" alt=\"$\\rho (r)\\propto r^{-\\gamma ^{\\prime }}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\rho (r)\\propto r^{-\\gamma ^{\\prime }}</script></span></span>). We adopt a uniform prior of 0.2 &#x2264; \u0393 &#x2264; 0.8. The projected axis ratio <em>b</em>/<em>a</em> has a uniform prior (0.3 &#x2264; <em>b</em>/<em>a</em> &#x2264; 1) with the position angle as a free parameter. The normalization of the mass profile is set by the Einstein radius \u03b8<sub>E</sub>, which is also a free parameter. We adopt a Gaussian prior on the mass centroid with a width of \u03c3 = 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />05 (see Koopmans et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r13\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r13\">2006</a>) that is centered on the fitted light centroid of the lens galaxy in the WFC3/F160W image (\u03bb<sub>rest</sub>\u2009 ~ \u20090.6\u2009\u03bcm).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjl497422f3\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjl497422f3\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422f3_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 3.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422f3_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 3.</strong>\u00a0Top row: negative <em>HST</em> images of the strong lensing system in the ACS/F475W, ACS/F814W, WFC3/F125W, and WFC3/F160W filters. The images are 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />62 on a side. The cyan cross denotes the centroid of the mass distribution, and the cyan circle the Einstein radius. Second row: images with the lens light subtracted. Only the pixels containing the lensed source are shown and used in the lens modeling. Third row: reconstructed image plane from the best-fit lens model. The model includes a compact emission region (point source convolved with the PSF) marked by the green cross. Fourth row: normalized image plane residuals where the color scale shows the \u00b12\u03c3 range. The green cross denotes the position of the compact source as in the third row. The magnification varies by ~0.5 over the region around the compact source. Grid lines are overplotted for clarity. The centroid of the lens light distribution in each filter (red cross) is offset from that of the mass (cyan cross). Bottom row: extended source reconstruction. The compact emission region is not reconstructed since it is unresolved, but its inferred location from the lens model is indicated (green cross). The source morphology is less constrained in the F125W and F160W because only the upper half-annulus is used in the model. The compact emission is offset from the source galaxy's center in all filters.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjl497422f3\" href=\"/2041-8205/789/2/L31/downloadFigure/figure/apjl497422f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjl497422f3\" href=\"/2041-8205/789/2/L31/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjl497422f3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>We first remove the lens galaxy's light using a single S\u00e9rsic profile, as this is sufficient to describe the lens light in the region of the lensed images. In F814W, we exclude the annular region containing the lensed images (objects A and B; Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl497422f2\">2</a>) when fitting the lens light profile. Because the lens is considerably brighter than the counterimage (object B; Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl497422f2\">2</a>) in F125W and F160W, we exclude only the half-annulus around arc A when fitting the lens light profile.</p><p>To constrain the lens mass parameters, we use image pixels in the annular regions in F475W and F814W and the half-annular regions in F125W and F160W (Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl497422f3\">3</a>, second row) that contain the lensed images. We construct weight images for each filter by adding Poisson noise from sources to the inverse variance images, as outlined in Koekemoer et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r12\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r12\">2011</a>) for CANDELS.\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">Glee</span> simultaneously models across the four bands and reconstructs the source onto a grid of 20 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 20 pixels with a resolution of ~0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />05. Our lens model also requires a point source convolved with the point-spread function (PSF) coincident with the peak surface brightness in image A (Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl497422f2\">2</a>). The position of this point source is the same across all filters and fit simultaneously with the lens model parameters. The counterimage of the point source is not modeled separately given its low magnification.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjl497422s3-2\" name=\"apjl497422s3-2\">3.2.\u00a0Modeling Lens Environment Contributions</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The lens galaxy is embedded in a cluster, and the overdense environment may affect the lens model (e.g., Momcheva et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r17\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r17\">2006</a>; Wong et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r39\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r39\">2011</a>). We model cluster galaxies within 2' of the lens as singular isothermal spheres truncated at <em>r</em><sub>200</sub> and estimate their virial masses assuming the stellar-to-halo mass relation of Moster et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r19\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r19\">2013</a>). We parameterize the cluster's dark matter halo as a spherical Navarro\u2013Frenk\u2013White (NFW) profile (Navarro et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r20\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r20\">1996</a>) with a mass of 7.7 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 10<sup>13</sup>\u2009<em>M</em><sub>\u2609</sub> centered at the peak of the X-ray emission (source 12A in Pierre et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r24\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r24\">2012</a>) and a concentration calculated using the mass\u2013concentration relation of Zhao et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r40\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r40\">2009</a>).</p><p>In addition to this fiducial model, we run an extensive suite of models to test environmental contributions to the lens. We explore multiple permutations with and without: (1) nearby cluster galaxies; (2) the cluster dark matter halo; (3) additional external shear; (4) galaxies along the line of sight, assumed to be in the lens plane. We also run test models that allow the cluster halo centroid to vary by the 25'' uncertainty on the X-ray emission centroid (Pierre et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r24\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r24\">2012</a>), as well as models where we double the cluster mass.</p><p>In exploring this wide variety of models, we find that they provide fits of comparable quality, and the inferred parameters (e.g., \u03b8<sub><em>E</em></sub>) among the different models agree to within their statistical uncertainties. We adopt our fiducial power-law ellipsoid lens model with a fixed NFW halo for the cluster and fixed isothermal halos for the cluster galaxies because it is realistic and has the fewest additional free parameters.</p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjl497422s4\" name=\"apjl497422s4\">4.\u00a0RESULTS</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"apjl497422s4-1\" name=\"apjl497422s4-1\">4.1.\u00a0Properties of the Lensing Galaxy</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>With our fiducial lens model, we measure an Einstein radius of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn10.gif\" alt=\"$\\theta _{\\rm E} = 0.38^{+0.02}_{-0.01}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\theta _{\\rm E} = 0.38^{+0.02}_{-0.01}</script></span></span> arcsec (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn11.gif\" alt=\"$3.2_{-0.1}^{+0.2}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">3.2_{-0.1}^{+0.2}</script></span></span>\u2009kpc) and total mass enclosed within \u03b8<sub>E</sub> of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn12.gif\" alt=\"$1.8^{+0.2}_{-0.1}\\times 10^{11}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">1.8^{+0.2}_{-0.1}\\times 10^{11}</script></span></span>\u2009<em>M</em><sub>\u2609</sub>. From our environment model, we estimate that the cluster halo and other cluster members contribute ~10% of this enclosed mass (~7% and ~3%, respectively), consistent with results at <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/lesssim.gif\" alt=\"lesssim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 0.5 (Treu et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r36\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r36\">2009</a>). Increasing the environment contribution would increase this fraction (e.g., a cluster halo with double the mass would contribute ~15% of the enclosed mass), but \u03b8<sub><em>E</em></sub> remains robust to within the model uncertainties. The lens galaxy's mass within \u03b8<sub>E</sub> is thus ~1.6 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 10<sup>11</sup>\u2009<em>M</em><sub>\u2609</sub>.</p><p>Following Papovich et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r22\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r22\">2012</a>), we now model the lens light in F160W with a two-component model using an <em>n</em> = 4 bulge and <em>n</em> = 1 disk. The arc is masked, although the source flux is negligible compared to the lens flux (&lt;3%). Papovich et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r22\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r22\">2012</a>) measure the total stellar mass assuming a Chabrier (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r5\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r5\">2003</a>) IMF with solar metallicity. We integrate the light profile and calculate the stellar mass within \u03b8<sub>E</sub> to be <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn13.gif\" alt=\"$1.3_{-0.2}^{+0.5} \\times 10^{11}\\, M_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">1.3_{-0.2}^{+0.5} \\times 10^{11}\\, M_{\\odot }</script></span></span>, corresponding to a dark matter fraction of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn14.gif\" alt=\"$f_{\\rm DM}^{{\\rm Chab}} {(&lt;} \\theta _{\\rm E}) = 0.3_{-0.3}^{+0.1}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">f_{\\rm DM}^{{\\rm Chab}} {(<} \\theta _{\\rm E}) = 0.3_{-0.3}^{+0.1}</script></span></span>. If we use a Salpeter (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r25\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r25\">1955</a>) IMF, which seems to be preferred for ETGs at <em>z</em> &lt; 1 (e.g., Auger et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r1\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r1\">2010</a>; Cappellari et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r4\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r4\">2012</a>; Sonnenfeld et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r28\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r28\">2012</a>; Conroy et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r6\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r6\">2013</a>), the enclosed stellar mass is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn15.gif\" alt=\"$2.2_{-0.4}^{+0.9} \\times 10^{11}\\, M_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">2.2_{-0.4}^{+0.9} \\times 10^{11}\\, M_{\\odot }</script></span></span> and is larger than the enclosed total mass (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn16.gif\" alt=\"$f_{\\rm DM}^{{\\rm Salp}} ({&lt;}\\theta _{\\rm E}) = -0.3_{-0.5}^{+0.2}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">f_{\\rm DM}^{{\\rm Salp}} ({<}\\theta _{\\rm E}) = -0.3_{-0.5}^{+0.2}</script></span></span>), albeit at marginal significance. This is an upper limit on the dark matter fraction of the galaxy, as the environment contributes ~10% of the total mass within \u03b8<sub>E</sub>.</p><p>In the three reddest filters (the lens is undetected in F475W), the centroids of the lens light profile and of the mass model are offset by as much as ~1.5 pixels (~0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />1; Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl497422f3\">3</a>). Studies of <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/lesssim.gif\" alt=\"lesssim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 0.5 ETGs do not find significant offsets between their mass and light (Koopmans et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r13\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r13\">2006</a>). However, the lens light centroid shifts among different bands, suggesting that the youngest stars are displaced from the older population. The different stellar populations may not all directly trace the dark matter.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjl497422s4-2\" name=\"apjl497422s4-2\">4.2.\u00a0Properties of the Lensed Source</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The source is magnified by a factor of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn17.gif\" alt=\"$2.1_{-0.3}^{+0.4}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">2.1_{-0.3}^{+0.4}</script></span></span>. The unlensed source has an extended profile with a bright compact region that is mapped to the outskirts of the source (Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl497422f3\">3</a>). We fit a S\u00e9rsic profile to the extended source to measure its flux. To compute the total flux (Table\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjl497422t1\">1</a>), we add the flux from the compact emission, which is determined by taking the flux of the fitted PSF component and dividing by the magnification at that location (|\u03bc<sub><em>A</em></sub>| in Table\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjl497422t1\">1</a>). We estimate the modeling uncertainty to be ~0.15\u2009mag by fitting to a subset of sources reconstructed from samples in the MCMC chain. Combined with the photometric uncertainties, the total uncertainty is ~0.2\u2009mag. The effective radius varies between <em>r</em><sub>eff</sub> ~ 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />11\u20130<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />20.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjl497422t1\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 1.</b>\u00a0Observed Quantitiesand Lens Model Parameters</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjl497422t1\" rowspan=\"1\">\u03b1, \u03b4 (J2000)</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\">02:18:21.5, \u221205:10:19.9</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\"><em>z</em><sub>L</sub> (mag)</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\">25.5 \u00b1 0.2</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\">ACS/F814W (mag)</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\">25.5 \u00b1 0.2</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\">WFC3/F125W (mag)</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\">25.9 \u00b1 0.2</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\">WFC3/F160W (mag)</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\">25.2 \u00b1 0.2</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table><p><small>\n<strong>Notes.</strong>\n<a name=\"apjl497422t1fn1\" id=\"apjl497422t1fn1\"></a><sup> a</sup>Total magnitudes from Skelton et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r27\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r27\">2014</a>).\n<a name=\"apjl497422t1fn2\" id=\"apjl497422t1fn2\"></a><sup> b</sup>Total stellar masses from Papovich et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r22\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r22\">2012</a>).\n<a name=\"apjl497422t1fn3\" id=\"apjl497422t1fn3\"></a><sup> c</sup>For lens model quantities, the reported values are medians, with errors corresponding to the 16th and 84th percentiles.\n<a name=\"apjl497422t1fn4\" id=\"apjl497422t1fn4\"></a><sup> d</sup>\u03bc<sub><em>A</em></sub>, \u03bc<sub><em>B</em></sub> are magnifications at the peak locations of the brighter and fainter images, respectively.\n<a name=\"apjl497422t1fn5\" id=\"apjl497422t1fn5\"></a><sup> e</sup>Offset of mass profile centroid relative to galaxy light centroid in F160W.\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n            Download table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/2041-8205/789/2/L31/suppdata/apjl497422t1_ascii.txt?doi=10.1088/2041-8205/789/2/L31\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/2041-8205/789/2/L31/suppdata/apjl497422t1_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>There is residual image flux (Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl497422f3\">3</a>, fourth row) that we attribute to compact emission regions in the source. The residuals shift in both intensity and position among the bands, likely because of different emission lines (Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl497422f1\">1</a>, bottom): F814W samples only the continuum and has the smallest residuals, while F475W has Ly\u03b1 and F160W has [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] \u03bb\u03bb4959, 5007 emission. Indeed, Ly\u03b1 emission can be spatially offset from continuum emission in galaxies at <em>z</em> &gt; 2 (e.g., Feldmeier et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r7\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r7\">2013</a>; Momose et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjl497422r18\" id=\"fnref-apjl497422r18\">2014</a>). We speculate that offset [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] \u03bb3727 emission may be causing the weaker residual feature in F125W. Although the G141 spectrum does not show it, [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>] \u03bb3727 would fall in a region where the grism response is dropping, making this interpretation uncertain. These residuals cannot come from the same source position, as lensing is achromatic. The lens model uses the same position of the compact emission region (green cross, Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl497422f3\">3</a>) across the multiple bands, but because they are offset, the model compromises by placing the PSF between the peak fluxes. This results in residuals in all bands, even F814W where there is only continuum.</p><p>The largest residual is in F475W and is due to Ly\u03b1 emission that is observed in both the arc and counterimage (objects A and B in Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl497422f2\">2</a>; see also Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjl497422f3\">3</a>, left). To test if the bright Ly\u03b1 emission is problematic for the lens modeling, we fit an additional PSF to the counterimage in F475W and subtract it a priori. Using only the upper half-annulus to model the lens, we find that the image residuals, inferred lens model parameters, and modeled source fluxes are nearly identical to that of our fiducial model.</p><p>The residuals corresponding to the emission-line regions extend in the direction of the arc (object A), i.e., tangential to the lens galaxy. This implies that the emission-line regions are elongated and/or stretched due to lensing.</p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjl497422s5\" name=\"apjl497422s5\">5.\u00a0CONCLUSIONS</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We report the discovery of the highest-redshift strong lensing galaxy known to date. The unusual gravitational lens is the most massive member of the galaxy cluster IRC 0218 at <em>z</em> = 1.62. We measure spectroscopic redshifts for the lens and source of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn43.gif\" alt=\"$z_{\\rm L}=1.6406^{+0.0018}_{-0.0050}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z_{\\rm L}=1.6406^{+0.0018}_{-0.0050}</script></span></span> and <em>z</em><sub>S</sub> = 2.2623 \u00b1 0.0002, respectively. Only with <em>HST</em>'s resolution are we able to separate the lensing BCG from the source, which is multiply imaged into a bright arc and a counterimage. The source shows strong Ly\u03b1 emission with an observed EW of 129.4 \u00b1 4.6\u2009\u00c5 as measured with Keck/LRIS.</p><p>We adopt a lens model that combines a power-law ellipsoid for the lens galaxy with an environmental component (fixed cluster NFW halo + isothermal halos for cluster galaxies). The Einstein radius is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn44.gif\" alt=\"$\\theta _{\\rm E}=0.38^{+0.02}_{-0.01}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\theta _{\\rm E}=0.38^{+0.02}_{-0.01}</script></span></span> arcsec (<span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn45.gif\" alt=\"$3.2_{-0.1}^{+0.2}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">3.2_{-0.1}^{+0.2}</script></span></span>\u2009kpc) and the total enclosed mass is <em>M</em><span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn46.gif\" alt=\"$_{\\rm tot}(&lt;\\theta _{\\rm E})=1.8^{+0.2}_{-0.1}\\times 10^{11}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">_{\\rm tot}(<\\theta _{\\rm E})=1.8^{+0.2}_{-0.1}\\times 10^{11}</script></span></span>\u2009<em>M</em><sub>\u2609</sub>. We estimate that the cluster environment contributes ~10% of this total mass. Assuming a Chabrier IMF for the lens galaxy, the enclosed stellar mass is <em>M</em><span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn47.gif\" alt=\"$_{\\star } ({&lt;} \\theta _{{\\rm E}}) = 1.3^{+0.5}_{-0.2} \\times 10^{11}\\, M_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">_{\\star } ({<} \\theta _{{\\rm E}}) = 1.3^{+0.5}_{-0.2} \\times 10^{11}\\, M_{\\odot }</script></span></span> and the upper limit on the galaxy dark matter fraction is <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn48.gif\" alt=\"$f_{\\rm DM}^{{\\rm Chab}} ({&lt;} \\theta _{\\rm E}) = 0.3_{-0.3}^{+0.1}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">f_{\\rm DM}^{{\\rm Chab}} ({<} \\theta _{\\rm E}) = 0.3_{-0.3}^{+0.1}</script></span></span>. Alternatively, a Salpeter IMF is marginally inconsistent with the enclosed mass, <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/2041-8205/789/2/L31/Full/apjl497422ieqn49.gif\" alt=\"$f_{\\rm DM}^{{\\rm Salp}} ({&lt;} \\theta _{\\rm E}) = -0.3_{-0.5}^{+0.2}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">f_{\\rm DM}^{{\\rm Salp}} ({<} \\theta _{\\rm E}) = -0.3_{-0.5}^{+0.2}</script></span></span>.</p><p>The reconstructed source has bright compact regions offset from the galaxy's center. These could be emission-line regions corresponding to Ly\u03b1 and [O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] \u03bb\u03bb4959, 5007 that likely probe different regions in the source.</p><p>Strong lensing galaxies at <em>z</em> &gt; 1 directly measure the stellar build-up of massive galaxies (e.g., whether the IMF evolves with redshift), and their number tests the current cosmological paradigm. Ongoing and upcoming deep imaging surveys should identify more lensing candidates to directly study the dark matter and light distributions of structures when the universe was ~30% of its current age.</p></div>\n<div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We thank Chuck Keeton and Curtis McCully for helpful discussions. K.C.W. is supported by an EACOA Fellowship awarded by the East Asia Core Observatories Association, which consists of the Academia Sinica Institute of Astronomy and Astrophysics, the National Astronomical Observatory of Japan, the National Astronomical Observatory of China, and the Korea Astronomy and Space Science Institute. This work was supported by a NASA Keck Award, administered by the NExSci, and data presented were obtained at the W. M. Keck Observatory from telescope time allocated to NASA through the partnership with the California Institute of Technology and the University of California. The observatory was made possible by the generous financial support of the W. M. Keck Foundation. The authors recognize and acknowledge the very significant cultural role and reverence that the summit of Mauna Kea has always had within the indigenous Hawaiian community. This work is based on observations taken with the NASA/ESA <em>HST</em> by the 3D-HST Treasury Program (GO 12177 and 12328), as well as by program GO 12590, supported by a NASA through a grant from the Space Telescope Science Institute. <em>HST</em> and STScI are operated by the Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy, Inc., under NASA contract NAS5-26555.</p></div></div><!-- End article full text -->\n<!-- Start Footnotes -->\n\t<h2 id=\"footnotes\">Footnotes</h2>\n\t\t<div data-mobile-collapse=\"\">\n\t\t\t<ul class=\"clear-list wd-content-footnotes\">\n\t\t\t\t<li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"apjl497422fn1\" id=\"apjl497422fn1\">*\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\"><p class=\"mb-0\"><p>Based on observations made with the NASA/ESA <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em>, obtained at the Space Telescope Science Institute, which is operated by the Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy, Inc., under NASA contract NAS 5-26555.            <div class=\"partner-logo-alignment\">\n                <!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/a56c0f0e-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/a56c0f0e-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<p></p>\n                </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n<!-- Branded journal header ends -->\n</div> <!-- end secondary-header -->\n<!-- Secondary header ends --><div class=\"da1-da2\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle\" id=\"page-content\">\n            <div class=\"da1 ta1 article-head\">\n                <!-- Start Eyebrow block, containing Surtitle and Labels -->\n<div class=\"eyebrow\">\n\t<!-- Start Collection Labels -->\n    <!-- End Collection Labels --> </div>\n<!-- End Eyebrow block -->\n\n<h1 itemprop=\"headline\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-title\">DISCOVERY OF A STRONG LENSING GALAXY EMBEDDED IN A CLUSTER AT <I>z</I> = 1.62<SUP>*</SUP>       </h1>\n\n<p class=\"mb-0\">\n\t<span data-authors=\"\">\n\t\t<span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">Kenneth C. End Email Alert -->\n<!-- End Email Alert --><!-- Start Citation Alert Link -->\n                        <p>\n<div class=\"jnl-notifications-wrapper\">\n    <a class=\"wd-jnl-email-alert\"
